## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of materials, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally-activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Johnson-Cook simplified (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * ((T - c4) * c5)**c6) (homologous temperature softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturation stress model)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * exp(-c3 * T) (saturation hardening with Arrhenius-type softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally-activated deformation)
- Swift equation: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (combined power hardening and linear softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear elastic-plastic transition)
- Exponential softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) (strain-temperature coupling with exponential thermal effect)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with thermal cross-term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T^n) or (c0 - c1*T) applied to stress expression
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally-activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c0/T) or exp(-c0*T) terms reflecting atomic-scale thermal activation
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress-strain relation representing initial yield strength before hardening
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as normalized form (T - c0)*c1 raised to a power, reflecting melting-point-referenced behavior
- Strain-temperature separability → Stress often factors as sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), where strain hardening and thermal softening are multiplicatively separable
- Power-law exponent range → Strain hardening exponent typically between 0.1 and 0.5 for metals, constraining c in epsilon**c
- Pre-strain or initial condition offset → (epsilon + c0) instead of epsilon alone, accounting for prior work hardening or initial dislocation density
